deprecate_posargs(deprecation_warning, remappable_names, /):\n101:     \"\"\"\n102:     Function/method decorator to deprecate some or all positional arguments.\n103: \n104:     The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n105:     the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n106: \n107:     The decorator takes two arguments: a RemovedInDjangoXXWarning warning\n108:     category and a list of parameter names that have been changed from\n109:     positional-or-keyword to keyword-only, in their original positional order.\n110: \n111:     Works on both functions and methods. To apply to a class constructor,\n112:     decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n113:     use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n114: \n115:     Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n116: \n117:         def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n118:             ...\n119: \n120:     to::\n121: \n122:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n123:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n124:             ...\n125: \n126:     After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n127: \n128:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n129:             ...\n130: \n131:     Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n132:     parameters or change the remaining ones. For example, this attempt to add a\n133:     new param would break code using the deprecated posargs::\n134: \n135:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n136:         def some_func(request, wrong_new_param=None, *, option1, option2=True):\n137:             # Broken: existing code may pass a value intended as option1 in the\n138:             # wrong_new_param position.\n139:             ...\n140: \n141:     However, it's acceptable to add new *keyword-only* parameters and to\n142:     re-order the existing ones, so long as the list passed to\n143:     @deprecate_posargs is kept in the original posargs order. This change will\n144:     work without breaking existing code::\n145: \n146:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n147:         def some_func(request, *, new_param=None, option2=True, option1):\n148:             ...\n149: \n150:     The @deprecate_posargs decorator adds a small amount of overhead. In most\n151:     cases it won't be significant, but use with care in performance-critical\n152:     code paths.\n153:     \"\"\"\n154: \n155:     def decorator(func):\n156:         if isinstance(func, type):\n157:             raise TypeError(\n158:                 \"@deprecate_posargs cannot be applied to a class. To avoid returning\\n313:         # an instance of a subclass, this function returns `bytes(value)`.\\n314:         # This doesn't make a copy when `value` already contains bytes.\\n315: \\n316:         # Handle string types -- we can't rely on force_bytes here because:\\n317:         # - Python attempts str conversion first\\n318:         # - when self._charset != 'utf-8' it re-encodes the content\\n319:         if isinstance(value, (bytes, memoryview)):\\n320:             return bytes(value)\\n321:         if isinstance(value, str):\\n322:             return bytes(value.encode(self.charset))\\n323:         # Handle non-string types.\\n324:         return str(value).encode(self.charset)\\n325: \\n326:     # These methods partially implement the file-like object interface.\\n327:     # See https://docs.python.org/library/io.html#io.IOBase\\n328: \\n329:     #
